              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37453672-sabrina?shelf=plot-holes-abound">plot-holes-abound</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37453672-sabrina?shelf=gross-out-relationships-or-sex">gross-out-relationships-or-sex</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1367933433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15716390470621873525">I hate to give this less than four stars but this is vastly inferior to its predecessor. It was likely written in haste and the author forgot what she wrote in the previous book. The characters went from being fully fleshed out and likable to one dimensional and annoying. Also stupid, they had brains and used them in the previous books but they have all been hit with a stupid stick here. They are shallow and act like children (their ages have frozen in time too even though years have passed) of </span>
  <span id="freeText15716390470621873525" style="display:none">I hate to give this less than four stars but this is vastly inferior to its predecessor. It was likely written in haste and the author forgot what she wrote in the previous book. The characters went from being fully fleshed out and likable to one dimensional and annoying. Also stupid, they had brains and used them in the previous books but they have all been hit with a stupid stick here. They are shallow and act like children (their ages have frozen in time too even though years have passed) of modern times instead of the semi-adults they used to be in a medieval setting.<br /><br />The story was spent mostly in the character Enna's head instead of on any actual linear story and most of those thoughts went like this....heat...fire....burn...I shouldn't burn things....but I want to burn things...burning things is bad....but I need to burn things...over and over and over again. I swear the author was going for a world record on how many times the words heat, burn and fire appear in a book. Every other sentence had at least one of those three words or more. Ugh.<br /><br />The romance presented was creepy as fuck too. A guy a decade older then our heroine sees her and becomes instantly obsessed with her and knows her secret of burning without any explanation. So he captures her, keeps her drugged and Stockholm syndrome sets in it gets gross. He then threatens her friend's lives and manipulates her into burning things for him. All the while the romance she had with a neighboring boy from the previous book is forgotten until close to the end and she is like, oh you like me? But we have been friends. I guess I like you to since you like me and tried to save me from creepy obsessive guy. We are in love! The secondary romance of the main character from the previous book was way over the top and not like it was either. To top that off we add pregnancy to the mix about which the woman is not concerned and often puts herself and the baby at risk and doesn't care. She must have forgotten she is the queen, the baby is the future heir and she is the smarter of the monarchs even if she is just a teenager and her husband is slightly older and actually raised to be king.<br /><br />This story could have been told in a lot less time and more orderly if the characters actually did what they talked about instead of saying what needs to happen, not doing it, denying it, running around doing things that make no sense and then finally doing what they said at the beginning of the book, it made 1/4 of the book quite tedious.<br /><br />Last where were all the adults? In a medieval setting where most characters acted and were treated like adults in the first book when they were young teens and there were adults, it seemed as if there was no one over their early twenties here and the young adults now acted like young teens or even preteens with no brains. Seriously there were 3 adults that I can think of in this entire story! The 3 adults lets the teens run everything without any input from someone with more experience or common sense. And the kingdoms are at war! Children fighting children in an all out war! It's a little too much.<br /><br />I will continue with this series however since I have been assured that the next book is back up to snuff and that this was the weakest of the series.<br /><br />Edit: The next book is a piece of shit, so much worse then this book. While the characters and situations here were a stretch the next book is annoying and unbelievable. I wanted to shake sense into the characters here, I wanted to kill them to put them out of their misery in the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15716390470621873525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_391486689" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/391486689" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4075354-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606221712p2/4075354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/391486689?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/4075354-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781934180570" href="/book/show/22546773-enna-burning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=from-library">from-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4075354-beth?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer391486689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2004692597472965009">I liked Enna Burning, but it just didn't come close to how much I loved the first book in the series, The Goose Girl. That one was a five star read for me. Enna Burning overall is a bit bleak, and I felt that the plot sort of dragged on in certain places. Though I didn't enjoy this one as much, there are still some beautiful passages and memorable characters. I like how it appears that all of the stories and characters are entwined, and I look forward to reading the next book in the series.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CWAPkV7AtTsl/FKVNRuzFK11G2kda2XHZu+3dprYyRszRmZD5Z58U4LX5vTC7rnLeyr8odPm66A9kfHHV5s7gQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('D/UZARgJZX8LqyjeuxXD5yeFmX+ZKMPDvV6fakJWlCY103DTo1esF6yAnL9M4Mk48dp+t1elTaTmINnbjxVmvA==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText4419285581791033007" style="display:none">Shannon Hale is the New York Times best-selling author of six young adult novels: the Newbery Honor book Princess Academy, multiple award winner Book of a Thousand Days, and the highly acclaimed Books of Bayern series. She has written three books for adults, including the upcoming Midnight in Austenland (Jan. 2012), companion book to Austenland. She co-wrote the hit graphic novel Rapunzel's Revenge and its sequel Calamity Jack with husband Dean Hale. They live near Salt Lake City, Utah with their four small children, and their pet, a small, plastic pig.</span>
